       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         Signature
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg">
          <img alt="Albert Einstein signature 1934.svg" data-file-height="88" data-file-width="585" height="23" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg/150px-Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg/225px-Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg/300px-Albert_Einstein_signature_1934.svg.png 2x" width="150"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Albert Einstein
       </b>
       (14 March 1879 – 18 April 1955) was a German-born
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theoretical_physicist" title="Theoretical physicist">
        theoretical physicist
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bio-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who developed the
       <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_relativity" title="Theory of relativity">
        theory of relativity
       </a>
       , one of the two pillars of
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">
        modern physics
       </a>
       (alongside
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">
        quantum mechanics
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-frs-5">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-YangHamilton2010_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-YangHamilton2010-7">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         274
        </span>
       </sup>
       His work is also known for its influence on the
       <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_science" title="Philosophy of science">
        philosophy of science
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He is best known by the general public for his
       <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass–energy equivalence">
        mass–energy equivalence
       </a>
       formula
       <span class="nowrap">
        <i>
         E
        </i>
        =
        <i>
         mc
        </i>
        <sup>
         2
        </sup>
       </span>
       (which has been dubbed "the world's most famous equation").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He received the 1921
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">
        Nobel Prize in Physics
       </a>
       "for his services to theoretical physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the
       <a href="/wiki/Photoelectric_effect" title="Photoelectric effect">
        photoelectric effect
       </a>
       ",
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a pivotal step in the evolution of
       <a href="/wiki/Introduction_to_quantum_mechanics" title="Introduction to quantum mechanics">
        quantum theory
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Near the beginning of his career, Einstein thought that
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newtonian_mechanics" title="Newtonian mechanics">
        Newtonian mechanics
       </a>
       was no longer enough to reconcile the laws of
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">
        classical mechanics
       </a>
       with the laws of the
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_field" title="Electromagnetic field">
        electromagnetic field
       </a>
       . This led him to develop his
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_theory_of_relativity" title="Special theory of relativity">
        special theory of relativity
       </a>
       during his time at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Patent_Office" title="Swiss Patent Office">
        Swiss Patent Office
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">
        Bern
       </a>
       (1902–1909), Switzerland. However, he realized that the principle of relativity could also be extended to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitational_fields" title="Gravitational fields">
        gravitational fields
       </a>
       and—with his subsequent theory of gravitation in 1916—he published a paper on
       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
        general relativity
       </a>
       . He continued to deal with problems of
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">
        statistical mechanics
       </a>
       and quantum theory, which led to his explanations of
       <a href="/wiki/Particle" title="Particle">
        particle
       </a>
       theory and the
       <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">
        motion of molecules
       </a>
       . He also investigated the thermal properties of light which laid the foundation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Photon" title="Photon">
        photon
       </a>
       theory of light. In 1917, he applied the general theory of relativity to model the large-scale structure of the
       <a href="/wiki/Universe" title="Universe">
        universe
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nobel-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20151124_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20151124-13">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1895 and 1914, he lived in Switzerland (except for one year in Prague, 1911–12), where he received his academic diploma from the
       <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">
        Swiss Federal Polytechnic
       </a>
       in Zürich (later the Eidgenössische Technische Hochschule, ETH) in 1900. He later taught at that institute as a professor of theoretical physics between 1912 and 1914 before he left for Berlin. In 1901, after being stateless for more than five years, he acquired
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_citizenship" title="Swiss citizenship">
        Swiss citizenship
       </a>
       , which he kept for the rest of his life. In 1905, he was awarded a PhD by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="University of Zürich">
        University of Zürich
       </a>
       . The same year, his
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Annus_mirabilis" title="Annus mirabilis">
         annus mirabilis
        </a>
       </i>
       (miracle year), he published
       <a href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers">
        four groundbreaking papers
       </a>
       , which were to bring him to the notice of the academic world, at the age of 26.
      </p>
      <p>
       He was visiting the United States when
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Adolf Hitler
       </a>
       came to power in 1933 and—being
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jewish
       </a>
       —did not go back to Germany, where he had been a professor at the
       <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Prussian Academy of Sciences">
        Berlin Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       . He settled in the United States, becoming an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_citizen" title="American citizen">
        American citizen
       </a>
       in 1940.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BoyerDubofsky2001_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BoyerDubofsky2001-14">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the eve of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , he endorsed a
       <a href="/wiki/Einstein%E2%80%93Szil%C3%A1rd_letter" title="Einstein–Szilárd letter">
        letter to President Franklin D. Roosevelt
       </a>
       alerting him to the potential development of "extremely powerful bombs of a new type" and recommending that the U.S. begin similar research. This eventually led to what would become the
       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">
        Manhattan Project
       </a>
       . Einstein supported defending the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
        Allied forces
       </a>
       , but generally denounced the idea of using the newly discovered
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">
        nuclear fission
       </a>
       as a weapon. Later, with the British philosopher
       <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Russell" title="Bertrand Russell">
        Bertrand Russell
       </a>
       , he signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Russell%E2%80%93Einstein_Manifesto" title="Russell–Einstein Manifesto">
        Russell–Einstein Manifesto
       </a>
       , which highlighted the danger of nuclear weapons. He was affiliated with the
       <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study" title="Institute for Advanced Study">
        Institute for Advanced Study
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Princeton,_New_Jersey" title="Princeton, New Jersey">
        Princeton, New Jersey
       </a>
       , until his death in 1955.
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein published
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_scientific_publications_by_Albert_Einstein" title="List of scientific publications by Albert Einstein">
        more than 300 scientific papers
       </a>
       along with over 150 non-scientific works.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nobel-12">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paul_Arthur_Schilpp,_editor_1951_730–746_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Paul_Arthur_Schilpp,_editor_1951_730–746-15">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His intellectual achievements and originality have made the word "
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Einstein#Noun" title="wikt:Einstein">
        Einstein
       </a>
       " synonymous with "
       <a href="/wiki/Genius" title="Genius">
        genius
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wordnetweb.princeton.edu_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wordnetweb.princeton.edu-16">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Wigner" title="Eugene Wigner">
        Eugene Wigner
       </a>
       wrote of Einstein in comparison to his contemporaries that "Einstein's understanding was deeper even than
       <a href="/wiki/John_von_Neumann" title="John von Neumann">
        Jansci von Neumann's
       </a>
       . His mind was both more penetrating and more original than von Neumann's. And that is a very remarkable statement."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">
        Life and career
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">
        Early life and education
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Einstein_family" title="Einstein family">
        Einstein family
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_(1882).jpg">
         <img alt="A young boy with short hair and a round face, wearing a white collar and large bow, with vest, coat, skirt and high boots. He is leaning against an ornate chair." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="414" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_%281882%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_at_the_age_of_three_(1882).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Einstein at the age of 3 in 1882
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg">
         <img alt="Studio photo of a boy seated in a relaxed posture and wearing a suit, posed in front of a backdrop of scenery." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="379" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_as_a_child.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Albert Einstein in 1893 (age 14)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_(color2).jpg">
         <img alt="Einstein's matriculation certificate at the age of 17. The heading reads &quot;The Education Committee of the Canton of Aargau&quot;. His scores were German 5, French 3, Italian 5, History 6, Geography 4, Algebra 6, Geometry 6, Descriptive Geometry 6, Physics 6, Chemistry 5, Natural History 5, Art Drawing 4, Technical Drawing 4. The scores are 6 = excellent, 5 = good, 4 = sufficient, 3 = poor, 2 = very poor, 1 = unusable." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2419" data-file-width="1479" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/170px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/255px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg/340px-Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_%28color2%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein%27s_exam_of_maturity_grades_(color2).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Einstein's matriculation certificate at the age of 17, showing his final grades from the Argovian cantonal school (
         <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alte_Kantonsschule_Aarau" title="de:Alte Kantonsschule Aarau">
          Aargauische Kantonsschule
         </a>
         , on a scale of 1–6, with 6 being the highest possible mark). He scored: German 5; French 3; Italian 5; History 6; Geography 4; Algebra 6; Geometry 6; Descriptive Geometry 6; Physics 6; Chemistry 5; Natural History 5; Art and Technical Drawing 4.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Albert Einstein was born in
       <a href="/wiki/Ulm" title="Ulm">
        Ulm
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Kingdom of Württemberg">
        Kingdom of Württemberg
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       , on 14 March 1879.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bio-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His parents were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hermann_Einstein" title="Hermann Einstein">
        Hermann Einstein
       </a>
       , a salesman and engineer, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pauline_Koch" title="Pauline Koch">
        Pauline Koch
       </a>
       . In 1880, the family moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">
        Munich
       </a>
       , where Einstein's father and his uncle Jakob founded
       <i>
        Elektrotechnische Fabrik J. Einstein &amp; Cie
       </i>
       , a company that manufactured electrical equipment based on
       <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">
        direct current
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bio_6-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bio-6">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Einsteins were non-observant
       <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">
        Ashkenazi Jews
       </a>
       and Albert attended a
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_school" title="Catholic school">
        Catholic elementary school
       </a>
       in Munich, from the age of 5, for three years. At the age of 8, he was transferred to the
       <a href="/wiki/Luitpold_Gymnasium" title="Luitpold Gymnasium">
        Luitpold Gymnasium
       </a>
       (now known as the Albert Einstein Gymnasium), where he received advanced primary and secondary school education until he left the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
        German Empire
       </a>
       seven years later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA59_59–61]_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA59_59–61]-18">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1894, Hermann and Jakob's company lost a bid to supply the city of Munich with electrical lighting because they lacked the capital to convert their equipment from the direct current (DC) standard to the more efficient
       <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">
        alternating current
       </a>
       (AC) standard.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The loss forced the sale of the Munich factory. In search of business, the Einstein family moved to Italy, first to
       <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">
        Milan
       </a>
       and a few months later to
       <a href="/wiki/Pavia" title="Pavia">
        Pavia
       </a>
       . When the family moved to Pavia, Einstein, then 15, stayed in Munich to finish his studies at the Luitpold Gymnasium. His father intended for him to pursue
       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">
        electrical engineering
       </a>
       , but Einstein clashed with authorities and resented the school's regimen and teaching method. He later wrote that the spirit of learning and creative thought was lost in strict
       <a href="/wiki/Rote_learning" title="Rote learning">
        rote learning
       </a>
       . At the end of December 1894, he travelled to Italy to join his family in Pavia, convincing the school to let him go by using a doctor's note.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199730–31_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199730–31-20">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During his time in Italy he wrote a short essay with the title "On the Investigation of the State of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aether_theories" title="Aether theories">
        Ether
       </a>
       in a Magnetic Field".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._5_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._5-21">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Contrary to popular mythology, Einstein always excelled at maths and physics from a young age, reaching a mathematical level years ahead of his peers. The twelve year old Einstein taught himself algebra and Euclidean geometry over a single summer. Einstein also independently discovered his own original proof of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem" title="Pythagorean theorem">
        Pythagorean theorem
       </a>
       at age 12.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A family tutor Max Talmud says that after he had given the 12 year old Einstein a geometry textbook, after a short time "[Einstein] had worked through the whole book. He thereupon devoted himself to higher mathematics... Soon the flight of his mathematical genius was so high I could not follow."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_page_17_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Einstein_page_17-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His passion for geometry and algebra led the twelve year old to become convinced that nature could be understood as a "mathematical structure".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_page_17_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Einstein_page_17-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Einstein started teaching himself calculus at 12, and as a 14 year old he says he had "mastered
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integral_calculus" title="Integral calculus">
        integral
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Differential_calculus" title="Differential calculus">
        differential
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">
        calculus
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At age 13, Einstein was introduced to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kant" title="Kant">
        Kant
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Critique_of_Pure_Reason" title="Critique of Pure Reason">
        Critique of Pure Reason
       </a>
       , and Kant became his favourite philosopher, his tutor stating: "At the time he was still a child, only thirteen years old, yet Kant's works, incomprehensible to ordinary mortals, seemed to be clear to him."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Einstein_page_17_24-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Einstein_page_17-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1895, at the age of 16, Einstein took the entrance examinations for the
       <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">
        Swiss Federal Polytechnic
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">
        Zürich
       </a>
       (later the Eidgenössische Technische Hochschule, ETH). He failed to reach the required standard in the general part of the examination,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_p._11_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_p._11-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but obtained exceptional grades in physics and mathematics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199736–37_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199736–37-27">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On the advice of the principal of the Polytechnic, he attended the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aargau" title="Aargau">
        Argovian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Mittelschule" title="Mittelschule">
        cantonal school
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">
        gymnasium
       </a>
       ) in
       <a href="/wiki/Aarau" title="Aarau">
        Aarau
       </a>
       , Switzerland, in 1895 and 1896 to complete his secondary schooling. While lodging with the family of professor Jost Winteler, he fell in love with Winteler's daughter, Marie. Albert's sister
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maja_Einstein" title="Maja Einstein">
        Maja
       </a>
       later married Winteler's son Paul.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter199321,_31,_56–57-28">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In January 1896, with his father's approval, Einstein renounced his
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_citizenship" title="German citizenship">
        citizenship in the German Kingdom of Württemberg
       </a>
       to avoid
       <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Germany" title="Conscription in Germany">
        military service
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199740_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199740-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September 1896, he passed the Swiss
       <a href="/wiki/Matura" title="Matura">
        Matura
       </a>
       with mostly good grades, including a top grade of 6 in physics and mathematical subjects, on a scale of 1–6.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_docs._21–27_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_docs._21–27-30">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At 17, he enrolled in the four-year mathematics and physics teaching diploma program at the Zürich Polytechnic. Marie Winteler, who was a year older, moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Olsberg,_Aargau" title="Olsberg, Aargau">
        Olsberg
       </a>
       , Switzerland, for a teaching post.
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein's future wife, a 20-year old
       <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
        Serbian
       </a>
       woman
       <a href="/wiki/Mileva_Mari%C4%87" title="Mileva Marić">
        Mileva Marić
       </a>
       , also enrolled at the Polytechnic that year. She was the only woman among the six students in the mathematics and physics section of the teaching diploma course. Over the next few years, Einstein and Marić's friendship developed into romance, and they read books together on extra-curricular physics in which Einstein was taking an increasing interest. In 1900, Einstein passed the exams in Maths and Physics and was awarded the Federal Polytechnic teaching diploma.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._67_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2008vol._1_(1987),_doc._67-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There have been claims that Marić collaborated with Einstein on his 1905 papers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers">
        <i>
         Annus Mirabilis
        </i>
        papers
       </a>
       , but historians of physics who have studied the issue find no evidence that she made any substantive contributions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPais19941–29_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPais19941–29-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA49_49–56]_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA49_49–56]-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marriages_and_children">
        Marriages and children
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_patentoffice.jpg">
         <img alt="Head and shoulders shot of a young, moustached man with dark, curly hair wearing a plaid suit and vest, striped shirt, and a dark tie." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="870" data-file-width="666" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/170px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/255px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Einstein_patentoffice.jpg/340px-Einstein_patentoffice.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_patentoffice.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Albert Einstein in 1904 (age 25)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The discovery and publication in 1987 of an early correspondence between Einstein and Marić revealed that they had had a daughter, called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieserl_Einstein" title="Lieserl Einstein">
        "Lieserl"
       </a>
       in their letters, born in early 1902 in
       <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">
        Novi Sad
       </a>
       where Marić was staying with her parents. Marić returned to Switzerland without the child, whose real name and fate are unknown. Einstein probably never saw his daughter. The contents of his letter to Marić in September 1903 suggest that the girl was either given up for adoption or died of
       <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_fever" title="Scarlet fever">
        scarlet fever
       </a>
       in infancy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg">
         <img alt="Einstein, looking relaxed and holding a pipe, stands next to a smiling, well-dressed Elsa who is wearing a fancy hat and fur wrap. She is looking at him." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1038" data-file-width="1200" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/220px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/330px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg/440px-Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein_Albert_Elsa_LOC_32096u.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Einstein with his second wife Elsa, 1921
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Einstein and Marić married in January 1903. In May 1904, their first son,
       <a href="/wiki/Hans_Albert_Einstein" title="Hans Albert Einstein">
        Hans Albert Einstein
       </a>
       , was born in
       <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">
        Bern
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       . Their second son,
       <a href="/wiki/Einstein_family#Eduard_&quot;Tete&quot;_Einstein_(Albert's_son)" title="Einstein family">
        Eduard
       </a>
       , was born in Zürich in July 1910. In April 1914 they moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
        Berlin
       </a>
       . After a few months, his wife returned to Zürich with their sons, after learning that Einstein's chief romantic attraction was his first and second cousin Elsa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel1966_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel1966-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They divorced on 14 February 1919, having lived apart for five years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA50_50]_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002[https://books.google.com/books?id=OAsQ_hFjhrAC&amp;pg=PA50_50]-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Eduard, whom his father called "Tete" (for
       <i>
        petit
       </i>
       ), had a breakdown at about age 20 and was diagnosed with
       <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">
        schizophrenia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson2015a_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Robinson2015a-42">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His mother cared for him and he was also committed to asylums for several periods, finally being committed permanently after her death.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeffe2007[https://books.google.com/books?id=B8K6n177ZwcC&amp;pg=PA203_203]_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeffe2007[https://books.google.com/books?id=B8K6n177ZwcC&amp;pg=PA203_203]-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In letters revealed in 2015, Einstein wrote to his early love, Marie Winteler, about his marriage and his still-strong feelings for her. In 1910, while his wife was pregnant with their second child, Einstein wrote to Marie that "I think of you in heartfelt love every spare minute and am so unhappy as only a man can be". Einstein spoke about a "misguided love" and a "missed life" regarding his love for Marie.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein married
       <a href="/wiki/Elsa_Einstein" title="Elsa Einstein">
        Elsa Löwenthal
       </a>
       in 1919,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007-45">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECalapriceKennefickSchulmann201562_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECalapriceKennefickSchulmann201562-46">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       after having had a personal relationship with her since 1912.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CalapriceLipscombe2005_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CalapriceLipscombe2005-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She was a first cousin maternally and a second cousin paternally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CalapriceLipscombe2005_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CalapriceLipscombe2005-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1933, they emigrated to the United States. In 1935, Elsa Einstein was diagnosed with heart and kidney problems; she died in December 1936.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter1993216_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHighfieldCarter1993216-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Friends">
        Friends
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Among Einstein's well-known friends were
       <a href="/wiki/Michele_Besso" title="Michele Besso">
        Michele Besso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ehrenfest" title="Paul Ehrenfest">
        Paul Ehrenfest
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann" title="Marcel Grossmann">
        Marcel Grossmann
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Plesch" title="János Plesch">
        János Plesch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Solovine" title="Maurice Solovine">
        Maurice Solovine
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Wise" title="Stephen Wise">
        Stephen Wise
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Patent_office">
        Patent office
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg">
         <img alt="Three young men in suits with high white collars and bow ties, sitting." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3396" data-file-width="4718" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/220px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/330px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg/440px-Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-with-habicht-and-solovine.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Olympia_Academy" title="Olympia Academy">
          Olympia Academy
         </a>
         founders:
         <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Habicht" title="Conrad Habicht">
          Conrad Habicht
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Solovine" title="Maurice Solovine">
          Maurice Solovine
         </a>
         and Einstein.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After graduating in 1900, Einstein spent almost two frustrating years searching for a teaching post. He acquired
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Swiss
       </a>
       citizenship in February 1901,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing199782_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing199782-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but was not
       <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Switzerland" title="Conscription in Switzerland">
        conscripted
       </a>
       for medical reasons. With the help of
       <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann" title="Marcel Grossmann">
        Marcel Grossmann
       </a>
       's father, he secured a job in
       <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">
        Bern
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Institute_of_Intellectual_Property" title="Swiss Federal Institute of Intellectual Property">
        Federal Office for Intellectual Property
       </a>
       , the patent office,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200763_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200763-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as an
       <a href="/wiki/Patent_examiner" title="Patent examiner">
        assistant examiner – level III
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGEFAQ_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IGEFAQ-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein evaluated
       <a href="/wiki/Patent_application" title="Patent application">
        patent applications
       </a>
       for a variety of devices including a gravel sorter and an electromechanical typewriter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGEFAQ_54-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-IGEFAQ-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1903, his position at the Swiss Patent Office became permanent, although he was passed over for promotion until he "fully mastered machine technology".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GalisonClock_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GalisonClock-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         370
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Much of his work at the patent office related to questions about transmission of electric signals and electrical-mechanical synchronization of time, two technical problems that show up conspicuously in the
       <a href="/wiki/Thought_experiment" title="Thought experiment">
        thought experiments
       </a>
       that eventually led Einstein to his radical conclusions about the nature of light and the fundamental connection between space and time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GalisonClock_55-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-GalisonClock-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         377
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With a few friends he had met in Bern, Einstein started a small discussion group in 1902, self-mockingly named "
       <a href="/wiki/Olympia_Academy" title="Olympia Academy">
        The Olympia Academy
       </a>
       ", which met regularly to discuss science and philosophy. Their readings included the works of
       <a href="/wiki/Henri_Poincar%C3%A9" title="Henri Poincaré">
        Henri Poincaré
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Mach" title="Ernst Mach">
        Ernst Mach
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/David_Hume" title="David Hume">
        David Hume
       </a>
       , which influenced his scientific and philosophical outlook.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200779-84_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson200779-84-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_scientific_papers">
        First scientific papers
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_(Nobel).png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="280" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png/170px-Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png/255px-Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/50/Albert_Einstein_%28Nobel%29.png 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_(Nobel).png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Einstein's official 1921 portrait after receiving the Nobel Prize in Physics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1900, Einstein's paper
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_scientific_publications_by_Albert_Einstein#Journal_articles" title="List of scientific publications by Albert Einstein">
        "Folgerungen aus den Capillaritätserscheinungen"
       </a>
       ("Conclusions from the Capillarity Phenomena") was published in the journal
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Annalen_der_Physik" title="Annalen der Physik">
         Annalen der Physik
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1901_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1901-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 30 April 1905, Einstein completed his thesis,
       <sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"_59-0'>
        <a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"-59'>
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner" title="Alfred Kleiner">
        Alfred Kleiner
       </a>
       , Professor of Experimental Physics, serving as
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pro_forma" title="Pro forma">
         pro-forma
        </a>
       </i>
       advisor. As a result, Einstein was awarded a PhD by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="University of Zürich">
        University of Zürich
       </a>
       , with his dissertation "
       <i>
        A New Determination of Molecular Dimensions
       </i>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"_59-1'>
        <a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1905b"Meinem_Freunde_Herr_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann_gewidmet_(Dedicated_to_my_friend,_Dr._Marcel_Grossmann)"-59'>
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"_60-0'>
        <a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1926bchap._"A_New_Determination_of_Molecular_Dimensions"-60'>
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In that same year, which has been called Einstein's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Annus_mirabilis" title="Annus mirabilis">
         annus mirabilis
        </a>
       </i>
       (miracle year), he published
       <a href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_papers" title="Annus Mirabilis papers">
        four groundbreaking papers
       </a>
       , on the photoelectric effect,
       <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">
        Brownian motion
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
        special relativity
       </a>
       , and the equivalence of mass and energy, which were to bring him to the notice of the academic world, at the age of 26.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_career">
        Academic career
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       By 1908, he was recognized as a leading scientist and was appointed lecturer at the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bern" title="University of Bern">
        University of Bern
       </a>
       . The following year, after giving a lecture on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrodynamics" title="Electrodynamics">
        electrodynamics
       </a>
       and the relativity principle at the University of Zürich,
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kleiner" title="Alfred Kleiner">
        Alfred Kleiner
       </a>
       recommended him to the faculty for a newly created professorship in theoretical physics. Einstein was appointed associate professor in 1909.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein became a full professor at the German
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles-Ferdinand_University" title="Charles-Ferdinand University">
        Charles-Ferdinand University
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">
        Prague
       </a>
       in April 1911, accepting
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austrian
       </a>
       citizenship in the
       <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">
        Austro-Hungarian Empire
       </a>
       to do so.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007164_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007164-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During his Prague stay, he wrote 11 scientific works, five of them on radiation mathematics and on the quantum theory of solids. In July 1912, he returned to his alma mater in Zürich. From 1912 until 1914, he was professor of theoretical physics at the
       <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">
        ETH Zurich
       </a>
       , where he taught analytical mechanics and
       <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamics" title="Thermodynamics">
        thermodynamics
       </a>
       . He also studied
       <a href="/wiki/Continuum_mechanics" title="Continuum mechanics">
        continuum mechanics
       </a>
       , the molecular theory of heat, and the problem of gravitation, on which he worked with mathematician and friend
       <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Grossmann" title="Marcel Grossmann">
        Marcel Grossmann
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 3 July 1913, he was voted for membership in the
       <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Prussian Academy of Sciences">
        Prussian Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       in Berlin.
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck" title="Max Planck">
        Max Planck
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Walther_Nernst" title="Walther Nernst">
        Walther Nernst
       </a>
       visited him the next week in Zurich to persuade him to join the academy, additionally offering him the post of director at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaiser_Wilhelm_Institute_for_Physics" title="Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics">
        Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics
       </a>
       , which was soon to be established.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStachel2002534-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Membership in the academy included paid salary and professorship without teaching duties at the
       <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">
        Humboldt University of Berlin
       </a>
       .) He was officially elected to the academy on 24 July, and he accepted to move to the German Empire the next year. His decision to move to Berlin was also influenced by the prospect of living near his cousin Elsa, with whom he had developed a romantic affair. He joined the academy and thus the Berlin University on 1 April 1914.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinstein201518–19_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinstein201518–19-66">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As World War I broke out that year, the plan for Kaiser Wilhelm Institute for Physics was aborted. The institute was established on 1 October 1917, with Einstein as its Director.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1916, Einstein was elected president of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Physical_Society" title="German Physical Society">
        German Physical Society
       </a>
       (1916–1918).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Based on calculations Einstein made in 1911, about his new theory of general relativity,
       <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_lens" title="Gravitational lens">
        light from another star should be bent
       </a>
       by the Sun's gravity. In 1919, that prediction was confirmed by Sir
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Eddington" title="Arthur Eddington">
        Arthur Eddington
       </a>
       during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_29_May_1919" title="Solar eclipse of 29 May 1919">
        solar eclipse of 29 May 1919
       </a>
       . Those observations were published in the international media, making Einstein world famous. On 7 November 1919, the leading British newspaper
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">
         The Times
        </a>
       </i>
       printed a banner headline that read: "Revolution in Science – New Theory of the Universe – Newtonian Ideas Overthrown".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eddington_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Eddington-69">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1920, he became a Foreign Member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences">
        Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1922, he was awarded the 1921
       <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">
        Nobel Prize in Physics
       </a>
       "for his services to Theoretical Physics, and especially for his discovery of the law of the photoelectric effect".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize-11">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the
       <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
        general theory of relativity
       </a>
       was still considered somewhat controversial, the citation also does not treat the cited work as an
       <i>
        explanation
       </i>
       but merely as a
       <i>
        discovery of the law
       </i>
       , as the idea of photons was considered outlandish and did not receive universal acceptance until the 1924 derivation of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planck_spectrum" title="Planck spectrum">
        Planck spectrum
       </a>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._N._Bose" title="S. N. Bose">
        S. N. Bose
       </a>
       . Einstein was elected a
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_1921" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 1921">
        Foreign Member of the Royal Society (ForMemRS) in 1921
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_5-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-frs-5">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He also received the
       <a href="/wiki/Copley_Medal" title="Copley Medal">
        Copley Medal
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">
        Royal Society
       </a>
       in 1925.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frs_5-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-frs-5">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="1921.E2.80.931922:_Travels_abroad">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1921–1922:_Travels_abroad">
        1921–1922: Travels abroad
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5008" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-220px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-330px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif/lossy-page1-440px-League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:League_of_Nations_Commission_067.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Albert Einstein at a session of the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation" title="International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation">
          International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
          League of Nations
         </a>
         ) of which he was a member from 1922 to 1932.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Einstein visited New York City for the first time on 2 April 1921, where he received an official welcome by Mayor
       <a href="/wiki/John_Francis_Hylan" title="John Francis Hylan">
        John Francis Hylan
       </a>
       , followed by three weeks of lectures and receptions. He went on to deliver several lectures at
       <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">
        Columbia University
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">
        Princeton University
       </a>
       , and in Washington he accompanied representatives of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Science" title="National Academy of Science">
        National Academy of Science
       </a>
       on a visit to the
       <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">
        White House
       </a>
       . On his return to Europe he was the guest of the British statesman and philosopher
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viscount_Haldane" title="Viscount Haldane">
        Viscount Haldane
       </a>
       in London, where he met several renowned scientific, intellectual and political figures, and delivered a lecture at
       <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King's College London">
        King's College London
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoffmann1972145–148_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoffmann1972145–148-71">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997499–508_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997499–508-72">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       He also published an essay, "My First Impression of the U.S.A.," in July 1921, in which he tried briefly to describe some characteristics of Americans, much as had
       <a href="/wiki/Alexis_de_Tocqueville" title="Alexis de Tocqueville">
        Alexis de Tocqueville
       </a>
       , who published his own impressions in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Democracy_in_America" title="Democracy in America">
         Democracy in America
        </a>
       </i>
       (1835).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For some of his observations, Einstein was clearly surprised: "What strikes a visitor is the joyous, positive attitude to life . . . The American is friendly, self-confident, optimistic, and without envy."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Holton-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         20
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1922, his travels took him to Asia and later to Palestine, as part of a six-month excursion and speaking tour, as he visited
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">
        Ceylon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japan
       </a>
       , where he gave a series of lectures to thousands of Japanese. After his first public lecture, he met the emperor and empress at the
       <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace" title="Tokyo Imperial Palace">
        Imperial Palace
       </a>
       , where thousands came to watch. In a letter to his sons, he described his impression of the Japanese as being modest, intelligent, considerate, and having a true feel for art.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307–308_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007307–308-75">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of Einstein's travels to the Far East, he was unable to personally accept the Nobel Prize for Physics at the Stockholm award ceremony in December 1922. In his place, the banquet speech was held by a German diplomat, who praised Einstein not only as a scientist but also as an international peacemaker and activist.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On his return voyage, he visited
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_for_Palestine" title="British Mandate for Palestine">
        Palestine
       </a>
       for 12 days in what would become his only visit to that region. He was greeted as if he were a head of state, rather than a physicist, which included a cannon salute upon arriving at the home of the British high commissioner,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Herbert_Samuel" title="Sir Herbert Samuel">
        Sir Herbert Samuel
       </a>
       . During one reception, the building was stormed by people who wanted to see and hear him. In Einstein's talk to the audience, he expressed happiness that the Jewish people were beginning to be recognized as a force in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007308_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007308-77">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Einstein visited Spain for two weeks in 1923, where he briefly met
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal" title="Santiago Ramón y Cajal">
        Santiago Ramón y Cajal
       </a>
       and also received a diploma from
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_XIII_of_Spain" title="Alfonso XIII of Spain">
        King Alfonso XIII
       </a>
       naming him a member of the Spanish Academy of Sciences.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1922 to 1932, Einstein was a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Intellectual_Cooperation" title="International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation">
        International Committee on Intellectual Cooperation
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
        Geneva
       </a>
       , a body created to promote international exchange between scientists, researchers, teachers, artists and intellectuals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Originally slated to serve as the Swiss delegate, Secretary-General
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eric_Drummond" title="Eric Drummond">
        Eric Drummond
       </a>
       was persuaded by Catholic activists
       <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Halecki" title="Oskar Halecki">
        Oskar Halecki
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Motta" title="Giuseppe Motta">
        Giuseppe Motta
       </a>
       to instead have him become the German delegate, thus allowing
       <a href="/wiki/Gonzague_de_Reynold" title="Gonzague de Reynold">
        Gonzague de Reynold
       </a>
       to take the Swiss spot, from which he promoted traditionalist Catholic values.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       His former physics professor
       <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Lorentz" title="Hendrik Lorentz">
        Hendrik Lorentz
       </a>
       and the French chemist
       <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">
        Marie Curie
       </a>
       were also members of the committee.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="1930.E2.80.931931:_Travel_to_the_U.S.">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1930–1931:_Travel_to_the_U.S.">
        1930–1931: Travel to the U.S.
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In December 1930, Einstein visited America for the second time, originally intended as a two-month working visit as a research fellow at the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">
        California Institute of Technology
       </a>
       . After the national attention he received during his first trip to the U.S., he and his arrangers aimed to protect his privacy. Although swamped with telegrams and invitations to receive awards or speak publicly, he declined them all.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007368_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007368-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After arriving in New York City, Einstein was taken to various places and events, including
       <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">
        Chinatown
       </a>
       , a lunch with the editors of the
       <i>
        New York Times
       </i>
       , and a performance of
       <i>
        Carmen
       </i>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">
        Metropolitan Opera
       </a>
       , where he was cheered by the audience on his arrival. During the days following, he was given the keys to the city by Mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Walker" title="Jimmy Walker">
        Jimmy Walker
       </a>
       and met the president of Columbia University, who described Einstein as "the ruling monarch of the mind".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Harry_Emerson_Fosdick" title="Harry Emerson Fosdick">
        Harry Emerson Fosdick
       </a>
       , pastor at New York's
       <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Church" title="Riverside Church">
        Riverside Church
       </a>
       , gave Einstein a tour of the church and showed him a full-size statue that the church made of Einstein, standing at the entrance.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_82-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also during his stay in New York, he joined a crowd of 15,000 people at
       <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">
        Madison Square Garden
       </a>
       during a
       <a href="/wiki/Hanukkah" title="Hanukkah">
        Hanukkah
       </a>
       celebration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370_82-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007370-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="1138" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/220px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/330px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg/440px-Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Einstein_and_Charlie_Chaplin_-_1931.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Einstein (left) and
         <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">
          Charlie Chaplin
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">
          Hollywood
         </a>
         premiere of
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">
           City Lights
          </a>
         </i>
         , January 1931
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Einstein next traveled to California, where he met
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caltech" title="Caltech">
        Caltech
       </a>
       president and Nobel laureate,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_A._Millikan" title="Robert A. Millikan">
        Robert A. Millikan
       </a>
       . His friendship with Millikan was "awkward", as Millikan "had a penchant for patriotic militarism," where Einstein was a pronounced
       <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">
        pacifist
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007373_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007373-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During an address to Caltech's students, Einstein noted that science was often inclined to do more harm than good.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This aversion to war also led Einstein to befriend author
       <a href="/wiki/Upton_Sinclair" title="Upton Sinclair">
        Upton Sinclair
       </a>
       and film star
       <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Chaplin" title="Charlie Chaplin">
        Charlie Chaplin
       </a>
       , both noted for their pacifism.
       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Laemmle" title="Carl Laemmle">
        Carl Laemmle
       </a>
       , head of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">
        Universal Studios
       </a>
       , gave Einstein a tour of his studio and introduced him to Chaplin. They had an instant rapport, with Chaplin inviting Einstein and his wife, Elsa, to his home for dinner. Chaplin said Einstein's outward persona, calm and gentle, seemed to conceal a "highly emotional temperament," from which came his "extraordinary intellectual energy".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaplin_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaplin-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         320
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Chaplin's film,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/City_Lights" title="City Lights">
         City Lights
        </a>
       </i>
       , was to premiere a few days later in Hollywood, and Chaplin invited Einstein and Elsa to join him as his special guests.
       <a href="/wiki/Walter_Isaacson" title="Walter Isaacson">
        Walter Isaacson
       </a>
       , Einstein's biographer, described this as "one of the most memorable scenes in the new era of celebrity".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374_84-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007374-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chaplin visited Einstein at his home on a later trip to Berlin, and recalled his "modest little flat" and the piano at which he had begun writing his theory. Chaplin speculated that it was "possibly used as kindling wood by the Nazis."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chaplin_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chaplin-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         322
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1933:_Emigration_to_the_U.S.">
        1933: Emigration to the U.S.
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-cartoon1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="624" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/220px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/330px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Einstein-cartoon1.jpg/440px-Einstein-cartoon1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein-cartoon1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cartoon of Einstein, who has shed his "Pacifism" wings, standing next to a pillar labeled "World Peace". He is rolling up his sleeves and holding a sword labeled "Preparedness" (by Charles R. Macauley, c. 1933).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In February 1933 while on a visit to the United States, Einstein knew he could not return to Germany with the rise to power of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazis
       </a>
       under Germany's new chancellor,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Adolf Hitler
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997659_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFölsing1997659-86">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007404_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007404-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       While at American universities in early 1933, he undertook his third two-month visiting professorship at the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">
        California Institute of Technology
       </a>
       in Pasadena. He and his wife Elsa returned to Belgium by ship in March, and during the trip they learned that their cottage was raided by the Nazis and his personal sailboat confiscated. Upon landing in
       <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">
        Antwerp
       </a>
       on 28 March, he immediately went to the German consulate and surrendered his passport, formally renouncing his German citizenship.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Nazis later sold his boat and converted his cottage into a
       <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">
        Hitler Youth
       </a>
       camp.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Refugee_status">
        Refugee status
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_landing_card_(5706142737).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="909" data-file-width="1391" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/220px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/330px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg/440px-Einstein%27s_landing_card_%285706142737%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einstein%27s_landing_card_(5706142737).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Albert Einstein's landing card (26 May 1933), when he landed in
         <a href="/wiki/Dover" title="Dover">
          Dover
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
          United Kingdom
         </a>
         ) from
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ostende" title="Ostende">
          Ostende
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
          Belgium
         </a>
         ) to visit
         <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">
          Oxford
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In April 1933, Einstein discovered that the new German government had passed laws barring Jews from holding any official positions, including teaching at universities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Historian
       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Holton" title="Gerald Holton">
        Gerald Holton
       </a>
       describes how, with "virtually no audible protest being raised by their colleagues", thousands of Jewish scientists were suddenly forced to give up their university positions and their names were removed from the rolls of institutions where they were employed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Holton_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Holton-74">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A month later, Einstein's works were among those targeted by the
       <a href="/wiki/German_Student_Union" title="German Student Union">
        German Student Union
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_book_burnings" title="Nazi book burnings">
        Nazi book burnings
       </a>
       , with Nazi propaganda minister
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Goebbels" title="Joseph Goebbels">
        Joseph Goebbels
       </a>
       proclaiming, "Jewish intellectualism is dead."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIsaacson2007407–410_88-2">
